  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0e5780cc-2fc1-43bd-835e-d171de9e4aae'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3396171470183030469"><b>
  <b>Sometimes you have to leave behind everything you know to find the place you truly belong...</b>
</b><br/><br/>Nana the cat is on a road trip. He is not sure where he's going or why, but it means that he gets to sit in the front seat of a silver van with his beloved owner, Satoru. Side by side, they cruise around Japan through the changing seasons, visiting Satoru's old friends. He meets</span>
  <span id="freeText3396171470183030469" style="display:none"><b>
  <b>Sometimes you have to leave behind everything you know to find the place you truly belong...</b>
</b><br /><br />Nana the cat is on a road trip. He is not sure where he's going or why, but it means that he gets to sit in the front seat of a silver van with his beloved owner, Satoru. Side by side, they cruise around Japan through the changing seasons, visiting Satoru's old friends. He meets Yoshimine, the brusque and unsentimental farmer for whom cats are just ratters; Sugi and Chikako, the warm-hearted couple who run a pet-friendly B&amp;B; and Kosuke, the mournful husband whose cat-loving wife has just left him. There's even a very special dog who forces Nana to reassess his disdain for the canine species. <br /><br />But what is the purpose of this road trip? And why is everyone so interested in Nana? Nana does not know and Satoru won't say. But when Nana finally works it out, his small heart will break...</span>
  <a data-text-id="3396171470183030469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_2437789996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2437789996" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2437789996?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451491336" href="/book/show/39508663-the-travelling-cat-chronicles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=berkleypub">berkleypub</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=received-to-review">received-to-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2437789996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9203090628707228362"><blockquote> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534428098i/26139834._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Humans who think we don't understand them are the stupid ones.</i>
</blockquote><b>Perfect. Absolutely perfect.</b><br/><br/>Hiro Arikawa is a masterful storyteller. I loved every word. I laughed, I cried, I was <b> an emotional whirlwind</b> in the best way possible. <br/><br/>Satoru, a young businessman, attempts to befriend a young feral cat with a crooked tail. <br/><br/>After a few weeks, the two work towards<b> a mutual understanding -</b> Satoru leaves "crunchies" for Nana and sometimes (only <i>sometimes</i>) Nana allows Satoru to pet him.<br/><br/>Then, something awful</span>
  <span id="freeText9203090628707228362" style="display:none"><blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534428098i/26139834._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Humans who think we don't understand them are the stupid ones.</i>
</blockquote><b>Perfect. Absolutely perfect.</b><br><br>Hiro Arikawa is a masterful storyteller. I loved every word. I laughed, I cried, I was <b> an emotional whirlwind</b> in the best way possible. <br><br>Satoru, a young businessman, attempts to befriend a young feral cat with a crooked tail. <br><br>After a few weeks, the two work towards<b> a mutual understanding -</b> Satoru leaves "crunchies" for Nana and sometimes (only <i>sometimes</i>) Nana allows Satoru to pet him.<br><br>Then, something awful happens - <b>Nana is struck by a car.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Somebody, help me! But that was idiotic. Nobody was going to help a stray.<br><br>Then, I remembered the man who came every night to leave me crunchies. Maybe he could help.</i>
</blockquote> Satoru hears Nana's painful yowls and rushes to help the injured cat. And thus begins one of <b>the greatest human-feline friendships </b>to have ever formed. <br><br>Only, five years later, Satoru packs everything into his car (including Nana) and sets off to <b>find Nana a new home.</b> Bewildered but determined, Nana knows one thing is for certain - no one will keep him from his human.<br><br>Wow - seriously wow - <b>this book was good.</b> I read it from cover to cover in a single afternoon and I'm itching for a re-read already!<br><br>Hiro Arikawa did an amazing job of writing from a cat's perspective. The combination of Nana's <b> hilarious derision</b> of humans:<blockquote>
  <i>Humans always underestimate our language skills. Just cause they can read and write, there's no need to act all high and mighty.</i>
</blockquote>and the author's <b>attention to detail</b> regarding Nana's thoughts and habits:<blockquote>
  <i>I yawned back. Sorry. Zero interest. Noriko just didn't get it. A wide box spoils all the fun; it offers none of the charms of being inside a box.</i>
</blockquote> really brought this book to life. I don't know how to explain it other than Nana <i>felt</i> like a real cat to me. <br><br>As Satoru attempts to find Nana a new home, he spends time with childhood friends. Inevitably, they begin to reminisce and the audience is treated with sweet, poignant and hilarious flashbacks (often with sarcastic commentary courtesy of Nana).<br><br>One of my favorite moments is how Satoru obtained Hatchi (his first cat). I don't want to spoil it, but it involved elementary kids running away, climbing a school building, leaning precariously over the roof and this quote: <blockquote>
  <i>Satoru turned to Kosuke with a grave expression on his face, "Kosuke, could you, like, kind of straddle the railing?"</i>
</blockquote> I honestly don't think this book could possibly be better. This is the kind of book that everyone should read at least once in their lifetimes.<blockquote>
  <i>Because it was a very special thing - to have your own cat in your home.</i>
</blockquote><i>With thanks to Berkley Publishing for an arc in exchange for an honest review<br><br>All quotes are from an uncorrected proof and are subject to change upon final publication</i><br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9203090628707228362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2570673062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16846777811265329343">I finished this book and closed it.<br/><br/>I immediately had chills all through my body.<br/><br/>This book is an excellent experience! The characters and the story will grab you from page one and won’t let you go. You will be told stories of good things and bad things, friendships and jealousy, family and heartbreak. Each of them, whether they bring sadness or joy will fill your heart and satisfy your mind.<br/><br/>While pets do play a key role in this story, I don’t think you need to be a pet lover to enjoy it. I am not</span>
  <span id="freeText16846777811265329343" style="display:none">I finished this book and closed it.<br /><br />I immediately had chills all through my body.<br /><br />This book is an excellent experience! The characters and the story will grab you from page one and won’t let you go. You will be told stories of good things and bad things, friendships and jealousy, family and heartbreak. Each of them, whether they bring sadness or joy will fill your heart and satisfy your mind.<br /><br />While pets do play a key role in this story, I don’t think you need to be a pet lover to enjoy it. I am not a big “fur baby” person myself, but I loved every single page of it. And, if you are a pet person, I think you will find even more satisfaction from this than I did. In fact, I find myself wanting to go out and get a cat now!<br /><br />Bring your Kleenex, you are going to need it!<br /><br />There is really nothing wrong with this book. It is absolutely perfect! It is going on my favorites list and I recommend it to all.<br /><br />Thank you so much to Berkley for providing me a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. I love when a publisher provides such great literature for me to read! <br /></span>

<div id="review_2146039908" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2146039908" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2146039908?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34728079-the-travelling-cat-chronicles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2146039908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12330596865675128569">This is a quirky, poignant and heartbreaking novel translated from the Japanese. There are the odd occasions at the beginning of this novel that you may think it is a trifle simplistic, but bear with it, as it will draw you in. It is related from the perspective of Satoru Miyawaki, and his beloved Nana, a stray cat, so named because his tail resembles the Japanese character for the number seven. Nana loved settling on Satoru's silver van, and found himself getting fed by him. He resembles a cat,</span>
  <span id="freeText12330596865675128569" style="display:none">This is a quirky, poignant and heartbreaking novel translated from the Japanese. There are the odd occasions at the beginning of this novel that you may think it is a trifle simplistic, but bear with it, as it will draw you in. It is related from the perspective of Satoru Miyawaki, and his beloved Nana, a stray cat, so named because his tail resembles the Japanese character for the number seven. Nana loved settling on Satoru's silver van, and found himself getting fed by him. He resembles a cat, Hachi, from Satoru's childhood. Nana is seriously injured in a car accident, makes his way to Satoru who gets him to a vet, and proceeds to nurse the cat for several months until he recovers. Feeling the depth of love that emanates from Satoru, the cat decides to stay. They have been happy together until the day Satoru embarks on a road trip to hand over Nana to one of his friends to look after as he is no longer in a position to look after him.<br /><br />Nana is puzzled as to why he is being given away, as indeed are Satoru's friends, there is some speculation as to whether he has lost his job, but they do not probe further. Their first stop is where Satoru grew up with his close friend, Kosuke, a cat lover with a difficult father and currently experiencing marital strife. Stories from their childhood include the wondrous running away from their parents incident orchestrated by Satoru in an attempt to manipulate Kosuke's father to accept a kitten, Hachi, which failed. Satoru takes in Hachi and the two were inseparable until circumstances precipitated Satoru's moving in with his aunt, Noriko, when Hachi is given to distant relatives. The visit ends with Satoru suggesting that Kosuke finding his own cat to lure his wife back. <br /><br />Noriko's job as a judge results in several moves and Satoru going to different high schools where he befriends Yoshimine, who is now farming and the next stop on the road trip. Yoshimine had parents who did not want him so he ends up living with his grandmother. The two were like brothers at school but manipulation ensures it will not be Nana's new home. Their next stop is near Mount Fuji, at Suki and Chikako's Hotel for Pets. Elements of their visit are strained with Suki comparing himself to Satoru, and finding himself wanting. This feeds his insecurities that his wife, Chikako, would have preferred Satoru rather than him. Once again circumstances conspire to ensure that Nana does not stay.<br /><br />The pair go on to see the glory and vibrancy of nature, the elemental force that is the sea and the graves of Satoru's parents. This is a story of a man and his cat, and what they will do to stay together for as long as is possible. It speaks of Satoru, his life, his friends and, above all else, his unbreakable bond with the wise and committed Nana. This is a gentle, yet utterly compelling read. Apparently this book has been a bestseller in Japan, and I can see why. A highly recommended read! Many thanks to Random House Transworld for an ARC.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12330596865675128569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Adina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22189348-adina"><img alt="Adina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531917330p2/22189348.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2116574668?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adina" href="/user/show/22189348-adina">Adina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34728079-the-travelling-cat-chronicles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22189348-adina?shelf=japan">japan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22189348-adina?shelf=cats">cats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22189348-adina?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2116574668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15382752740730023959">I decided to read this small novel because I recently adopted a lovely kitten and the blurb promised a “tender feel-good story of a man's journey around Japan with a streetcat. ” As I feel nothing but love for my fur ball, I thought this was going to be the perfect companion for the moments Arya decides to sleep in my lap and I have to keep still 2 hours so I do not disturb the princess. It started as promised, a funny story from the cat’s perspective but then it became a bitter-sweet account of</span>
  <span id="freeText15382752740730023959" style="display:none">I decided to read this small novel because I recently adopted a lovely kitten and the blurb promised a “tender feel-good story of a man's journey around Japan with a streetcat. ” As I feel nothing but love for my fur ball, I thought this was going to be the perfect companion for the moments Arya decides to sleep in my lap and I have to keep still 2 hours so I do not disturb the princess. It started as promised, a funny story from the cat’s perspective but then it became a bitter-sweet account of friendship, loss and love. And the ending, well, it broke my heart in million tiny pieces. I read the last pages on the plane and I was pretending to look out of the window so the other passengers would not see the tears streaming down my face. I probably should have expected this since the writer is Japanese and I am yet to read an entirely joyful novel coming from that country.<br><br>The novel starts in the mind of a successfully stray male cat that starts to accept food from a kind-hearted stranger. After he is badly injured by a car, he is taken in by the cat-lover and soon becomes a beloved pet to Satoru Miyawaki. They become increasingly attached with one another and it comes as a surprise when Satoru begins to search for someone to adopt the cat, now named Nana, because he was unable to keep her any longer. The 2 companions embark on a trip along the Japanese islands (unsuccessfully) searching for the perfect human replacement. It becomes the perfect pretext to visit old friends from Satoru’s past and re-live important moments from his childhood. <br><br>Nana’s voice is exactly as I imagine a cat talk. Ironic, witty, straight forward, overconfident and reluctant to fully admit its feelings of love for his human companion. The cat’s nuggets of wisdom are mingled with a 3rd person account of the trip and the recollection of Satoru’s relationship history with each person they visit. <br><br>Although in the beginning the prose feels very simple and naive, it soon becomes clear that it is a bit more than a feel-good story about a cat and her master. It was sweet, endearing and sad as I learned more about Satoru’s childhood and I started to guess the reason he had to abnadon his dear furry friend. <br><br>Although they were a tear jerker, I still loved Satoru and Nana’s adventures and I warmly recommend this novel to anyone with a heart and love for animals. <br><br>I thank Netgalley, Hiro Arikawa and Random House UK, Transworld Publishers for providing me with a copy in exchange for my honest review. <br><br>P.S. Here’s a pic with my little one. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511181902i/24489449._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2563812778" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2563812778" />
    <a title="Mischenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko"><img alt="Mischenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587209348p2/1194517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2563812778?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2563812778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14586004585584998802"><a href='http://i.imgur.com/rXnCjEK' title='' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1540407034i/26494995._SX540_.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The story begins with a stray cat who enjoys being free and is very happy with his life. His favorite place to sleep is on top of a parked, silver van that belongs to a young man named Satoru. Satoru likes the cat and brings him ‘crunchies’ from time to time. Eventually, the cat suffers an injury and needs some help.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>“By the time I reached the silver van, dawn was breaking. I really couldn’t take another step. This is it, I thought. I cried out at the top of my lungs. Oww…owwwww!”</b>
</i><br/><br/>Luckily,</span>
  <span id="freeText14586004585584998802" style="display:none"><a href="http://i.imgur.com/rXnCjEK" title="" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1540407034i/26494995._SX540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The story begins with a stray cat who enjoys being free and is very happy with his life. His favorite place to sleep is on top of a parked, silver van that belongs to a young man named Satoru. Satoru likes the cat and brings him ‘crunchies’ from time to time. Eventually, the cat suffers an injury and needs some help.<br><br><i>
  <b>“By the time I reached the silver van, dawn was breaking. I really couldn’t take another step. This is it, I thought. I cried out at the top of my lungs. Oww…owwwww!”</b>
</i><br><br>Luckily, Satoru comes to his rescue, takes him in as his pet, and a beautiful relationship begins to develop between the two. He names the cat Nana and they become best friends.<br><br>Years later, Satoru tells Nana that they’re going on a road trip together. He has to find a new home for Nana and it’s unknown exactly why. On the trip they visit each of Satoru’s friends around Japan and it’s like a trip down memory lane.<br><br><i>
  <b>“It seemed Satoru wanted me to go with him somewhere. He opened the door of my basket and I got in without making a fuss. For the five years I’d lived with him, I’d always been a sensible cat. For instance, even when he took me to my bête noire, the vet, I didn’t make a racket.”</b>
</i><br><br>When it’s time for Nana to stay at his new home, it’s something he’s not willing to accept. In Nana’s eyes, Satoru is his home and the only one he’s willing to accept.<br><br>The story started out slow and seemed too simple at first. I had some issues with the dialogue/narration in the beginning and had a hard time getting into it. I realized that I just needed to slow down, and once I settled in, it was hard to put the book down. It was around the last half of the book that literally had me captivated with all the beautiful scenery and adventures they took together. As the story unfolded, I had so many emotions. It’s been awhile since I’ve had to walk away from a book multiple times to bawl my eyes out! Other times, I found Nana hilarious as he reminded me of my old, wise, outdoor cat, Rambo. How Nana talks is how I imagine the animals in my life think. As a pet owner in general, I reflected greatly when reading this story as it reminded me of the unconditional love we have for each other.<br><br>Overall, this story is truly written beautifully and I thought the epilogue wrapped it up perfectly. Honestly, I don’t think you have to be a cat lover to enjoy this book. I’d recommend it to anyone. Also, I was very excited to learn that the book has been adapted to film and can’t wait to watch it!<br><br>4.5****<br><br>I’d like to thank Elisha at Berkley Publishing Group and the author Hiro Arikawa for sharing this book with me in exchange for an honest review.<br><br>You can also see this review @ <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://readrantrockandroll.com/2018/10/24/book-review-the-traveling-cat-chronicles-by-hiro-arikawa-bookreview-berkleypub/">https://readrantrockandroll.com/2018/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14586004585584998802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2451271013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2451271013" />
    <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea"><img alt="Amalia Gkavea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559158764p2/56789747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2451271013?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amalia Gkavea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amalia Gkavea" href="/user/show/56789747-amalia-gkavea">Amalia Gkavea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34728079-the-travelling-cat-chronicles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=world-literature">world-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56789747-amalia-gkavea?shelf=japan">japan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2451271013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13419311491975539779"><i> <b>‘’Human beings are basically huge monkeys that walk upright, but they can be pretty full of themselves.’’</b></i><br/><br/>Confession alert: each time I see a cat- and I literally mean EACH time- I shout ‘’Kitty!’’ at the top of my lungs like a 5-year-old who has never seen a cat before or like a 33-year-old cat idiot, which is precisely what I am. Unashamedly. I adore all animals but cats are one of my major weaknesses. Furthermore, Greeks love cats and the beautiful felines are one of the attractions of Atheni</span>
  <span id="freeText13419311491975539779" style="display:none"><i> <b>‘’Human beings are basically huge monkeys that walk upright, but they can be pretty full of themselves.’’</b></i><br /><br />Confession alert: each time I see a cat- and I literally mean EACH time- I shout ‘’Kitty!’’ at the top of my lungs like a 5-year-old who has never seen a cat before or like a 33-year-old cat idiot, which is precisely what I am. Unashamedly. I adore all animals but cats are one of my major weaknesses. Furthermore, Greeks love cats and the beautiful felines are one of the attractions of Athenian neighborhoods and every village in Greece, so there is no escaping my adoration in the all-holy Cat shrine. Now, this bubbling means that I absolutely loved, no, adored Hiro Arikawa’s marvelous gem of a novel.<br /><br /><i> <b>‘’I know this is a bit sudden, but could you take my cat for me?’’</b></i><br /><br />The novel starts with a male, sassy and hugely intelligent cat commenting on the things that make felines utterly majestic. Accurate. The - yet unnamed - feline meets Satoru, a young man who is a cat fanatic through and through. Satoru becomes his owner, names him Nana and the once stray angel becomes an adored pet. However, after five years, Satoru is unable to keep him. So, the two protagonists start a journey through Japan and through Satoru’s childhood memories to find the most suitable (and fortunate) owner for Nana. These are their stories…<br /><br /><i> <b>The Husband Without A Life</b></i>: Satoru’s most beloved childhood friend, Kozuke, is the first candidate. A young man who has marital problems that go back a turbulent relationship with his tyrannical father. This isn’t just a story of Kozuke but also a vital insight into Satoru’s past and a sad, yet tender, chapter.<br /><i> <b>The Unsentimental Farmer</b></i>: A former classmate who loves nature and knows how to talk straight, an honest soul, is Satoru’s next destination. This chapter is dominated by a super wonderful grandma.<br /><br /><i> <b>‘’Relax with your beloved pet while enjoying a breathtaking view of mount Fuji.’’</b></i><br /><br /><i> <b>Sugi and Chikako’s Hotel For Pets</b></i>: This is a lovely scenery, is it not? Here, we have a beautiful setting, a sassy, sexy female feline, a weird dog and a marriage plagued by jealousy. Not sure whether Nana could put up with all these at the same time.<br /><br /><i> <b>‘’I don’t get why humans like to have a huge stone put on top of them when they kick the bucket.’’</b></i><br /><br /><i> <b>Between Friends</b></i>: Now, we travel to Hokkaido, in a chapter that is actually a celebration of the nature of Japan. One of my favourite moments in the book.<br /><i> <b>How Noriko Learned to Love</b></i>: In the final journey, we are taken to Sapporo to meet Satoru’s aunt, Noriko. A fascinating, difficult, remarkable woman and a revelation that left me speechless. I froze. Those of you who have read the book will surely know what I’m talking about.<br /><br /><i> <b>‘’It’s called Nana. After the shape of his tail, like a seven.’’</b></i><br />As Adina write in her beautiful review, this novel is a symphony of excellent, fascinating notes. First of all, Arikawa has done a tremendous job in depicting how a sassy, genius cat would speak, how it must think and behave. Satoru is a wonderful character and this novel is full of rich, memorable characters. I could see every cat lover in him. However, the wealth of the Japanese setting becomes a character on its own. Japanese stories and traditions, the sea and the mountains. The glimpses in certain well-known Japanese values, from work ethic and the ‘’crime’’ of breaking the rules to the art of decluttering. <br /><br />There is an underlying sadness throughout the story, along with hope and love. However, I felt that the presence of loss and death was too powerful to overcome. This isn’t a cute, happy story that has a talking cat as a protagonist. Far from it and if you go into the book expecting this, then you’ll be disappointed. This is a poignant, difficult, powerful journey of understanding yourself and, most importantly, the others. Of the bravery we need to unearth once we’re faced with impossible choices and irreversible situations. Having a cat as a company makes everything a little bit better.<br /><br /><i> <b>‘’As we count up the memories from one journey, we head off on another.<br />Remembering those who went ahead. Remembering those who will follow after’’</b></i><br /><br />My reviews can also be found on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://theopinionatedreaderblog.wordpress.com">https://theopinionatedreaderblog.word...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13419311491975539779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2601754303" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2601754303" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2601754303?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451491336" href="/book/show/39508663-the-travelling-cat-chronicles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10171516-jessica?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2601754303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10991772444686732109"><b>
  <i>'as we count up the memories from one journey, we head off on another. remembering those who went ahead. remembering those who will follow after. and someday, we will meet all those people again, out beyond the horizon.'</i>
</b><br/><br/>oh my goodness. who would expect such a tiny book to contain so much <i>e m o t i o n</i>?!<br/><br/>as a (previous) long-time cat owner, this book is something that i can relate to on somewhat of an instinctual level. from recognising nanas various moods to empathising with satoru for how mu</span>
  <span id="freeText10991772444686732109" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>'as we count up the memories from one journey, we head off on another. remembering those who went ahead. remembering those who will follow after. and someday, we will meet all those people again, out beyond the horizon.'</i>
</b><br /><br />oh my goodness. who would expect such a tiny book to contain so much <i>e m o t i o n</i>?!<br /><br />as a (previous) long-time cat owner, this book is something that i can relate to on somewhat of an instinctual level. from recognising nanas various moods to empathising with satoru for how much he loves nana, its feels like once youre a cat person, you will always be a cat person. <br /><br />but i am positive that other pet owners will be able to relate to this story, as well. by accompanying a man and his cat on their journey across japan, the reader is able to understand that even if the destination changes, home will always be where the heart is. and sometimes your heart is simply given to a pet. <br /><br />having just reached the one year anniversary of losing my cat, a little fur ball who had unconditionally been by my side for 16 years, this is a story that i really needed to read and one i know i will visit countless times throughout my life. because, sometimes, reading about a cat on an adventure is exactly what is needed to cheer the soul. &lt;3<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10991772444686732109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2606027141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2606027141" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2606027141?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=cultural">cultural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=cloud-library">cloud-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=animals-and-pets">animals-and-pets</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2606027141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8081584897991967171">The Travelling Cat Chronicles by Hiro Arikawa, Philip Gabriel (Translator) is a 2018 Viking publication. (Originally published in 2012). <br/><br/>An emotional, poignant story featuring an amazing cat named Nana-<br/> <br/>Nana is a stray cat who enjoys sleeping in the sun on the hood of a van, and tolerating humans if necessary, especially if he is given crunchy bits to eat. <br/><br/>But, when tragedy strikes, by way of getting hit by a car, Nana is taken in by the human, Satoru, the van owner who leaves him food. Satoru n</span>
  <span id="freeText8081584897991967171" style="display:none">The Travelling Cat Chronicles by Hiro Arikawa, Philip Gabriel (Translator) is a 2018 Viking publication. (Originally published in 2012). <br /><br />An emotional, poignant story featuring an amazing cat named Nana-<br /> <br />Nana is a stray cat who enjoys sleeping in the sun on the hood of a van, and tolerating humans if necessary, especially if he is given crunchy bits to eat. <br /><br />But, when tragedy strikes, by way of getting hit by a car, Nana is taken in by the human, Satoru, the van owner who leaves him food. Satoru names him Nana, because his crooked tail is shaped like the Japanese number seven. They have some great times together, but suddenly, after several years, Satoru, must re-home his beloved cat. <br /><br />So, he goes on a journey with Nana, to find him a new home. <br /><br />The journey takes us back in time to Satoru’s childhood where we learn about his life and his friendships and relationship with a cat he knew before he had Nana, for whom he still mourns. He gets to reconnect with old friends, but has a hard time finding someone who can take Nana. <br /><br />Nana is our storyteller and narrates this journey in a way only a cat could. If you are a cat lover, you will know exactly what I mean. Nana, of course, knows in his infinite wisdom, the lessons that will enlighten Satoru, and the reader, upon his journey. <br /><br />This is such a wonderful fable, despite the tearjerker premise, centering on friendship, and human connections. Satoru may have led a life of isolation, but he is a such a warm -hearted man, and of course I recognized in him a fellow ‘cat person’, which endeared him to me, even more. But, perhaps to those who may feel cats are too aloof for your taste, this book dispels that notion, in countless ways. <br /><br />We realize right away that Satoru is helping Nana, taking care of him even before his accident, giving him a very nice, pampered life. We see what a gentle soul, he is, despite some very difficult times in his life. But it is what Nana does for Satoru that is at the heart of the story. What Satoru learns on their journey and how Nana remains his best friend, is loyal to him in all ways, and eternally grateful, will bring tears to your eyes. <br /><br />Yes, this story is sentimental and bittersweet, but the message is profound, despite or maybe because of its simplicity, and will resonate with pet lovers of all stripes, but certainly to those who have a truly special bond with their feline companions.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8081584897991967171" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2435145054?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela M" href="/user/show/4685500-angela-m">Angela M</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451491336" href="/book/show/39508663-the-travelling-cat-chronicles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4685500-angela-m?shelf=netgalley-reviews">netgalley-reviews</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2435145054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17063228939105605551">3.5 stars <br/>I wasn’t going to read this book. I’m not a cat person. I’m not a dog person either. In all honesty, I’m just not an animal person, although I do find kittens and puppies to be adorable. I hope all my pet loving friends won’t judge me - it’s just the way I am. But I couldn’t ignore all of the wonderful reviews that talked about what a lovely story this was and I’m glad I didn’t skip it . A lonely man Satoru adopts a stray cat, a feisty, sometimes sarcastic, sometimes sweet and always l</span>
  <span id="freeText17063228939105605551" style="display:none">3.5 stars <br />I wasn’t going to read this book. I’m not a cat person. I’m not a dog person either. In all honesty, I’m just not an animal person, although I do find kittens and puppies to be adorable. I hope all my pet loving friends won’t judge me - it’s just the way I am. But I couldn’t ignore all of the wonderful reviews that talked about what a lovely story this was and I’m glad I didn’t skip it . A lonely man Satoru adopts a stray cat, a feisty, sometimes sarcastic, sometimes sweet and always loyal cat. We know this because Nana, as he is named, is the narrator of this story. The two connect or rather I should say Nana connects with Satoru when Satoru cares for him after he is hit by a car. Satoru was already taken with Nana, leaving food as Nana camped out by Satoru silver van. We later discover that he loved a different cat when he was a young boy. And thus begins their friendship. <br /><br />Five years later they embark on a journey across Japan as Satoru is seeking a new home for Nana. On their travels, it is eventually revealed why Satoru is trying to find a new home for his beloved cat. It is through this journey that we come to know Satoru and through his visits with friends from his childhood and his aunt, we learn things haven’t always been easy for him. It’s a quick read that is simply written, sentimental, sweet and sad. The writing felt a little too simplistic at times, but perhaps it’s because it’s a translation. You don’t have to be a cat lover to feel the heart in this story about companionship, compassion, acceptance, loss and how to say goodbye<br /><br />I received an advanced copy of this book from Berkeley through NetGalley. Thanks Elisha !</span>
  <a data-text-id="17063228939105605551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2483232077" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2483232077" />
    <a title="Susanne  Strong" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4514828-susanne-strong"><img alt="Susanne  Strong" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583087410p2/4514828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2483232077?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susanne  Strong" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susanne  Strong" href="/user/show/4514828-susanne-strong">Susanne  Strong</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=2018-five-star-books">2018-five-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=direct-from-publisher">direct-from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4514828-susanne-strong?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2483232077" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3757283529149370954"><b>5 Stars.<br/><br/>Bittersweet, Lovely & Poignant.<br/><br/>Somethings in life are Kismet. Nana, meeting Saturo is exactly that.</b> <br/><br/>Nana, is a street cat - completely happy with his life: his favorite place to chill is under the hood of a silver van. Saturo’s van. When he was a boy, Saturo had a cat that looked just like Nana - that cat’s name was Hachi and Saturo loved him very much. Nana of course, wants nothing to do with Saturo - though he sure does like the crunchy food he leaves for him!<br/><br/>Then the worst thing imagi</span>
  <span id="freeText3757283529149370954" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars.<br /><br />Bittersweet, Lovely &amp; Poignant.<br /><br />Somethings in life are Kismet. Nana, meeting Saturo is exactly that.</b> <br /><br />Nana, is a street cat - completely happy with his life: his favorite place to chill is under the hood of a silver van. Saturo’s van. When he was a boy, Saturo had a cat that looked just like Nana - that cat’s name was Hachi and Saturo loved him very much. Nana of course, wants nothing to do with Saturo - though he sure does like the crunchy food he leaves for him!<br /><br />Then the worst thing imaginable happens - Nana gets hit by a car! Being a street cat he has no idea what he’s going to do.. And then it comes to him .. If I make enough noise, howling, “Oww!, Oww! ..” I cried out at the top of my lungs… “Oww.. Owww!!.. “ ..Saturo might just help and well, it works. And that my friends is how Nana become Saturo’s cat. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Listen cat, I was wondering if you would like to become my cat?” Saturo asks. As for names..”How about Nana?” “What?” Your tail “hooks in the opposite direction from Hachi’s and from the top it looks like nana, the number seven.” “Now wait just a second. Isn’t Nana a girl’s name. I’m a full fledged, hot blooded male..” “You’re okay with that, aren’t you, Nana?” “Do you like the name?” Nope! But well. Asking that while stroking my chin, is playing foul. I purred in spite of myself. “So you like it. Great” I told you already, I do not. </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />As the years go by they become quite the pair, inseparable - doing everything together. Nana however does whatever he has to to make sure that Saturo knows that Nana is the boss, as all cats are. Then one day Saturo suggests they take a journey to visit some of his former school friends. The reason? Saturo needs to find Nana new home and he won’t give Nana or anyone else a reason.<br /><br />On this journey spanning several beautiful towns in and around Japan, Nana meets Kosuke. Kosuke misses his wife desperately. He is hoping that having a cat will bring her back to him. Saturo thinks Nana is perfect for Kosuke, Nana however, has other ideas. Yoshimine is a farmer. He is a little rough around the edges and is looking for a proper cat. Yoshimine just found a little kitten who has no idea how to be a cat, thus Nana takes it upon himself to teach the kittie how to act. Thereafter Saturo is shocked when the kittie acts out in a way that makes it impossible for Yoshimine to take Nana! The next stop is Sugi and Chikago’s Hotel for Pets. Sugi and Chikago allow dogs and cats to stay along with their owners. Saturo is therefore convinced that this must be the place! Imagine his surprise when Sugi’s normally calm submissive dog shows an intense dislike for Nana. Whatever is going on?!<br /><br />Nana loves his master wholeheartedly and does not want to find a new home. For Nana, home is with Saturo, whose only remaining option is to stay with his Aunt Noriko, the same aunt who would not let Saturo keep Hachi when he was younger. Now however, Noriko wants to be there for her nephew and in turn, for Nana.<br /><br /><b>“The Travelling Cat Chronicles” is an amusing, sad and poignant story about the unconditional love formed between pets and their parents. It is the story of life. How seemingly beautiful and unfair it can be at the same time. Much of it is told from Nana’s perspective and there were times that I laughed as Nana is quite a funny quirky little cat, and there were times that I cried, tears welling up in my eyes, threatening to spill over. </b><br /><br />Written by Hiro Arikawa, published in Japanese and translated to English by Philip Gabriel, “The Travelling Cat Chronicles” is beautifully written. It is both humorous and heartbreaking and is filled with gorgeous descriptions I was able to imagine quite vividly. The story of Saturo and Nana will stay with me, their bond and their love for each other is sweet, solid and simply perfect. <br /><br />“The Travelling Cat Chronicles” was offered to me by Elisha at Berkley Publishing Group, three days after I adopted my first cat. Talk about Kismet! Having always been a dog person previously, this was a big decision for me. When I received this offer, I just knew this would be a special book for me and I was right. I waited a few weeks to read it as I wanted to discover what my own cat’s habits were like so that I would have a point of reference for Nana which made this book that much more special. I smile just thinking about Nana, his love for Saturo, and Saturo’s love for Nana. As far as I’m concerned, there’s nothing quite like the unconditional love given to a human by their pet and “The Travelling Cat Chronicles” is a prime example of unconditional love at its best.<br /><br />Thank you to Elisha at Berkley Publishing Group and Hiro Arikawa for an ARC of this novel in exchange for an honest review. Elisha - your offering this to me when you did made my day.<br /><br />Published on Goodreads and Twitter on 8.26.18. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3757283529149370954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451491336" href="/book/show/39508663-the-travelling-cat-chronicles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2423494698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3040328121875876286"> ***NOW AVAILABLE***<br/><br/><br/>This is a bit of a slow starter but by the first 100 pages the beautiful prose had me in it’s hands. Being a cat lover and owner I jumped at the chance to read and review this beautiful little book, I was not disappointed.<br/><br/>This is not a book to be rushed. It is best read when you have time to savor the story and the sentiment that is being relayed. The novel is told in alternating perspectives by Satoru Miyawaki and his much loved cat, Nana. Although a male, Nana was named for</span>
  <span id="freeText3040328121875876286" style="display:none"> ***NOW AVAILABLE***<br /><br /><br />This is a bit of a slow starter but by the first 100 pages the beautiful prose had me in it’s hands. Being a cat lover and owner I jumped at the chance to read and review this beautiful little book, I was not disappointed.<br /><br />This is not a book to be rushed. It is best read when you have time to savor the story and the sentiment that is being relayed. The novel is told in alternating perspectives by Satoru Miyawaki and his much loved cat, Nana. Although a male, Nana was named for the Japanese character for the number seven, which is what the shape of his tale looks like. <br /><br />Having had cats for over 48 years, the voice of this cat really sounded like something a cat would think. This probably sounds funny to anyone who has never had a relationship with a cat but they are indeed intelligent, gentle and very responsive to the feelings of the humans that they love and that is just how Nana comes across. So many of the things told from his perspective made me laugh and his love for Satoru was forever. <br /><br />The beginning of their bond starts in the first half of the book, from Satoru starting to feed Nana who was then a stray until she is injured and needs help. Once taken in by Satoru, Nana is quite overcome with the kindness, comfort and love that Satoru offers. That’s why he is confused when they set off on a journey, apparently to find a new home for Nana. We will come to learn why later in the story.<br /><br />The story of Satoru’s childhood and early life are revealed as we visit one friend after another looking for the perfect next home for Nana. Satoru doesn’t reveal his reasons for this, just states that he will no longer be able to take care of Nana. During their long journey they stop at many beautiful sites, the first of which is Mount Fuji. Nana states “I wonder how many cats in Japan have see the actual Mount Fuji . . . . .Our silver van was like a magic carriage. Every time I got into it, it carried me to a place I’d never been before. At that moment, we were without doubt the greatest travelers in the world. And I was the world’s greatest traveling cat.”<br /><br />I will leave you to discover the rest of this beautiful story, there is much to be learned about friendship, love, family and relationships from this book. It is definitely one that I will purchase upon it’s release in October, 2018. <br /><br />I received an ARC of this novel from Edelweiss.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3040328121875876286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2424004357" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2424004357" />
    <a title="Cheri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/106692-cheri"><img alt="Cheri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601402708p2/106692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2424004357?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheri" href="/user/show/106692-cheri">Cheri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451491336" href="/book/show/39508663-the-travelling-cat-chronicles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=japan">japan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=publisher-berkley-publishing-group">publisher-berkley-publishing-group</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=cats">cats</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=pets">pets</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2424004357" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6660139071250808720"><i>”Time, I've been passing time<br/>Watching trains go by.<br/>All of my life, <br/>Lying on the sand watching seabirds fly.<br/>Wishing there would be<br/>Someone waiting home for me.<br/><br/>“Something's telling me it might be you<br/>It's telling me it might be you<br/>All of my life...”</i><br/><br/>--<i>”It Might Be You,”</i> Stephen Bishop, Songwriters: Alan Bergman / Dave Grusin / Marilyn Bergman<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ILbe2DAs39M'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ILbe2...</a> or<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Y9AVoIROBt0'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Y9AVo...</a> (Tootsie - 1982)<br/><br/>When first we meet Nana, he is a relaying the story of how he</span>
  <span id="freeText6660139071250808720" style="display:none"><i>”Time, I've been passing time<br />Watching trains go by.<br />All of my life, <br />Lying on the sand watching seabirds fly.<br />Wishing there would be<br />Someone waiting home for me.<br /><br />“Something's telling me it might be you<br />It's telling me it might be you<br />All of my life...”</i><br /><br />--<i>”It Might Be You,”</i> Stephen Bishop, Songwriters: Alan Bergman / Dave Grusin / Marilyn Bergman<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ILbe2DAs39M">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ILbe2...</a> or<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Y9AVoIROBt0">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Y9AVo...</a> (Tootsie - 1982)<br /><br />When first we meet Nana, he is a relaying the story of how he came to be given his name, how he lived as a stray cat, sleeping on the hood of a silver van in a parking lot of an apartment building, until one day he is curled up, snoozing when he feels eyes upon him. Satoru asks him if he always sleeps there, ends up offering him some chicken, sneaks in a soft scratching of his chin to his ears, and just when he’s ready to let Satoru know that enough’s enough, Satoru says he’ll see him later as he walks away.<br /><br />They continue like this for a while, Satoru leaving him handfuls of crunchy cat food. Still, Nana knows better than to rely on a human, so he still needs to maintain his survival skills and connections. And so he heads out one night and fate intervenes, and he ends up hurt by a car. He drags his hurt leg back close to the silver van, howling <i>”oww owwww”</i> all the way; hoping the man with the food would help. <br /><br />Satoru hears the howling and comes down, sees his hurt leg and picks him up to put him in the van, all the while talking to him, asking him what happened, and does it hurt, and if he really was calling for him, as Satoru already believes. And so a bond has been formed, and when Nana is ready to leave the vet, Satoru brings him home to his apartment to recover. <br /><br />Satoru hasn’t had a cat since he was a young boy, his cat Hachi had to go live elsewhere, and Satoru still retains the scars of that trauma. There is something about this cat that makes him ask if he would like to become <i>his</i> cat, and a bond is formed. <br /><br />Of course, now that they have agreed on this arrangement, Satoru must find a name for this cat, who reminds him of his beloved Hachi, named for the Japanese word for the number eight, so named for the markings on his head. And so he names his new cat Nana, because <i>na</i> is the Japanese character for the number seven, which resembles the shape of Nana’s tail. <br /> <br />Days and weeks and months pass, and eventually years have passed. It is time for a journey; one they will take together to visit three of Satoru’s longstanding friends. It is a journey neither will ever forget. <br /><br />Neither will I.<br /><br />I especially loved the parts of this story that were narrated by Nana, and watching the evolution of him as he goes from people-wary and scavenging for food to allowing himself the joy of being loved, and as a result learns the value and joy of both giving and receiving love. I loved his sense of humour, his sharp and clever vision of their daily journey through life together.<br /><br />This begins slowly, but it is beautifully told, translated from Japanese by Philip Gabriel, charming without being twee, a loving and lovely bond between two beings, neither asking nor expecting more than the other can give. Each one willing to sacrifice for the happiness of the other, sharing their lives, watching the continually changing landscape as the journey takes them from place to place. It is lovely, quirky, tender, touching and heartbreaking, and a tribute to the bonds between man and his best friend, be it one that walks on two legs or four.<br /><br />A charming, lovely and compassionate vision of a quietly contemplative man and his companion, a man whose very life has been a portrait of humane and gentle consideration for all, and his feline friend who is committed, determined, to stay by his side until the laws of nature deem otherwise. <br /><br /><i>Tissues may be required</i><br /><br /><br /><br />Pub Date: 23 OCT 2018<br /><br />Many thanks for the ARC provided by Berkley Publishing Group</span>

<div id="review_2570245683" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2570245683" />
    <a title="Debra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5032725-debra"><img alt="Debra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525132364p2/5032725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2570245683?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debra" href="/user/show/5032725-debra">Debra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5032725-debra?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5032725-debra?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2570245683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12427889682062282180">4.5 Stars<br/><br/>"On our last journey, let's see all kinds of amazing things. Let’s spend our time taking in as many wonderful sights as we can."<br/><br/>Satoru has found and befriended a stray cat who he later names Nana. Nana reminds him of a cat, Hatchi, he had as a child. As he beings to feed Nana his "crunchies", they slowly develop an affinity for each other. After Nana is hit by a car, Satoru brings him home and the two live a happy life together. Until....<br/><br/>"I know this is a bit sudden, but can you take my</span>
  <span id="freeText12427889682062282180" style="display:none">4.5 Stars<br /><br />"On our last journey, let's see all kinds of amazing things. Let’s spend our time taking in as many wonderful sights as we can."<br /><br />Satoru has found and befriended a stray cat who he later names Nana. Nana reminds him of a cat, Hatchi, he had as a child. As he beings to feed Nana his "crunchies", they slowly develop an affinity for each other. After Nana is hit by a car, Satoru brings him home and the two live a happy life together. Until....<br /><br />"I know this is a bit sudden, but can you take my cat for me?"<br /><br />After five years of living together, Satoru is looking for a new home for Nana. As the two travel in a sliver van across Japan, they will see many wondrous sights and meet important people from Satoru's childhood. As they make stops at many of Satoru's friends’ homes, the reader is given glimpses into Satoru's childhood and his loving and tender nature. With each stop, Nana makes an impression and makes it known that he does not want to be apart from Satoru. Each has found the other. Each has benefited from their relationship. They are lonely, they are loyal, they are a pair, they will pull on your heartstrings, they might make you cry.<br /><br />"Don't leave me... Stay with me."<br /> "I will never, ever, leave him."<br /><br /><br />Why is Satoru looking for a new home for Nana? Will he find a new home? Will Nana stay with Satoru? This wonderful little gem of a book is full of heart. I guessed why Satoru was looking for a new home for Nana, the cat named because of the shape of his tail. The story tells of their time together and is complimented with the insightful thoughts of Nana the cat. Through the story, Nana gives his point of view, his opinions and often converses with other animals. He attempts to teach a kitten how to hunt and be a "cat", he talks to dog's and the reader is privy to his thoughts about his owner and those they meet. I loved how the Author captured Nana's spirit and his feline behaviors such as preference for boxes, food, affection and how he is touched. Pets are family members and I loved how the Author showed this in the book. Satoru and Nana loved each other and their devotion and loyalty to each other was evident.<br /><br />This is a touching tale of love, acceptance, finding a home, making a home and saying goodbye. Keep some tissues on hand as this book pulls at the heartstrings. It is easy to care for both Satoru and Nana. <br /><br />Beautiful, heartbreaking, hopeful and Satisfying.<br /><br />Highly Recommend.<br /><br />Thank you to Berkley Publishing Group and NetGalley who provided me with a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. All the thoughts and opinions expressed in this review are my own.<br /><br />Read more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.openbookpost.com">www.openbookpost.com</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2567469579?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2018</a>

        <a title="Berit☀️✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Berit☀️✨" href="/user/show/38946743-berit">Berit☀️✨</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38946743-berit?shelf=book-besties">book-besties</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2567469579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10323987488915616800">A beautifully told, heartwarming story, that will make you never look at your cat the same way again....<br/><br/>Do you ever wonder what your cat is thinking? Especially when he gives you one of those looks, you know the one! In this charming story guaranteed to put a smile on your face you will get the perspective of Nana, The cat and his owner Satoru... there is a sweet innocence to this book that will melt even the hardiest of hearts.... cat person, dog person, it doesn’t matter this is a book perfect</span>
  <span id="freeText10323987488915616800" style="display:none">A beautifully told, heartwarming story, that will make you never look at your cat the same way again....<br /><br />Do you ever wonder what your cat is thinking? Especially when he gives you one of those looks, you know the one! In this charming story guaranteed to put a smile on your face you will get the perspective of Nana, The cat and his owner Satoru... there is a sweet innocence to this book that will melt even the hardiest of hearts.... cat person, dog person, it doesn’t matter this is a book perfect for all human people....<br /><br />Nana is a content stray who is befriended by Satoru.... their relationship is limited to Satoru giving him crunchies, until one day Nana is injured and needs his friend... from there a beautiful relationship blooms between man and cat.... then one day Satoru takes Nana on a road trip, determined to find the perfect New home... but Nana is confused, why must Satoru find him a new home?<br /><br />The quest for Nana‘s new home takes the two of them on a journey down memory lane... I loved all The people they met along the road trip, I loved all the back stories, and learning about Satoru’s childhood.... but most of all I love Nana’s insight and snarky comments... what a brilliant cat with a quick tongue and a heart of gold... at its very core this book really is about the unconditional love between people and their pets.... it is about the impact we have on other peoples lives however insignificant we might think it is... it is about kindness, heart, hope, and compassion....<br /><br />This is a refreshing story, unlike anything I have ever read... it will rejuvenate your Faith in all species big and small... A book that will break your heart and then build you back up and fill you with hope!<br /><br />Absolutely recommend to anyone who enjoys a good story, with well developed characters, that will both inspire you and comfort you...<br /><br />*** A huge thank you too Berkley for my copy of this book ***</span>

  <span id="freeText3149383241412665837" style="display:none">Nana is a stray cat who, when injured by a car, is taken in by a kind man Satoru. <span id="freeTextContainer14965937916470461413"><b>5 sentimental stars to The Travelling Cat Chronicles!</b> 🐱 🐱 🐱 🐱 🐱 <br/><br/>If you are an animal lover, read this book.   <span id="freeText14965937916470461413" style="display:none"><b>5 sentimental stars to The Travelling Cat Chronicles!</b> 🐱 🐱 🐱 🐱 🐱 <br /><br />If you are an animal lover, read this book. Especially if you are a cat lover, don’t miss it! If you enjoy a sentimental, loving, perfectly told story, I implore you to read The Travelling Cat Chronicles!<br /><br />From the beginning, when I read Nana’s voice, I knew the author, Hiro Arikawa, has been loved by a cat. We’ve all read the story about “man’s best friend,” the dog, but what about the love of a cat? <br /><br />Nana is a stray cat living in a parking garage who slowly becomes affiliated with the owner of a van he sleeps on. The owner, Satoru, begins feeding him, and when Nana is hit by a car, he needs help. Satoru rescues him, and Nana becomes his cat. They live together happily for several years. <br /><br />Much later, Satoru takes Nana on a road trip to see several of his childhood friends, and all the while Nana is wondering what is happening because it appears Satoru is searching for a new home for him. <br /><br />The Travelling Cat Chronicles is storytelling perfection. Curl up with this book, and I promise you, you will devour it in one afternoon. It is heartfelt, poignant, endearing, and everything you could want in a book. <br /><br />On a personal note, Nana loves his Satoru the way I believe my cat loves me, and to feel that devotion through Nana’s voice is one of the most masterful things I’ve read in a work of fiction. <br /><br />Thank you to Berkley for the complimentary ARC and the blog tour invite. All opinions are my own. <br /><br />My reviews can also be found on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jennifertarheelreader.com">www.jennifertarheelreader.com</a></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
