        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2846301937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16812832960751205629">My 1500th review!<br/><br/>This is the heart-opening story of Nana, a stray cat who finds a master, Satoru, to whom he grows close until Satoru cannot keep him anymore and the two of them travel in search of a new home, visiting friend after friend, reminiscing, making realizations and growing closer still. The more people Satoru and Nana visit, the more we understand about these two characters (especially their pasts and personalities) and many more.<br/><br/>I found this story very unique. I had never read a book</span>
  <span id="freeText16812832960751205629" style="display:none">My 1500th review!<br /><br />This is the heart-opening story of Nana, a stray cat who finds a master, Satoru, to whom he grows close until Satoru cannot keep him anymore and the two of them travel in search of a new home, visiting friend after friend, reminiscing, making realizations and growing closer still. The more people Satoru and Nana visit, the more we understand about these two characters (especially their pasts and personalities) and many more.<br /><br />I found this story very unique. I had never read a book about an animal before, an animal who shares his thoughts with the reader in such a way that I personally believed Nana to be real and an intelligent creature who is capable of full sentences. I call this a ‘‘heart-opening story’’ because it truly opens your heart wide to welcome these wonderful characters and emotional situations. <br /><br />The writing is on the slow and dry side, despite the emotional content, which is why I won’t give this a five-star rating, but the story is whimsical, memorable and just all kinds of beautiful. I’m more of a dog person but the author almost convinced me that cats are worth adopting and loving until the day you die. There’s still doubt in my mind but here I am looking at cats differently—with more love and respect.<br /><br />Read it. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

<div id="review_2569534959" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2569534959" />
    <a title="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books"><img alt="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562505567p2/57632045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2569534959?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" href="/user/show/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books">Mackenzie - PhDiva Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books?shelf=book-besties">book-besties</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2569534959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9597210196447809222">Emotional, charming, and heartwarming. I don’t know that there is a better way to describe this book other than absolutely perfect. Nana the cat charmed me and seeing the world through his eyes simply filled me with laughs, tears, and smiles. I highly recommend this book to anyone who could use some healing of the soul. It reminded me about love, and being caring, and doing something for others even if it is hard. It’s a book of lessons told in a beautiful story form. I imagine this might be the</span>
  <span id="freeText9597210196447809222" style="display:none">Emotional, charming, and heartwarming. I don’t know that there is a better way to describe this book other than absolutely perfect. Nana the cat charmed me and seeing the world through his eyes simply filled me with laughs, tears, and smiles. I highly recommend this book to anyone who could use some healing of the soul. It reminded me about love, and being caring, and doing something for others even if it is hard. It’s a book of lessons told in a beautiful story form. I imagine this might be the type of book that every reader experiences a little bit differently, and has a slightly different “aha!” moment from. But I can’t imagine a reader on this earth whose heart won’t warm at this beautiful book!<br /><br /><b>About the Book</b><br /><br /><i>“I am a cat. As yet, I have no name.”</i><br /><br />Before he became Nana, he was a stray cat living on the streets and scrounging for food. He loved sleeping on the hood of a silver van, for it attracted the sunlight and warmed his belly, even in the cold winter. But he didn’t have a name. Not until Satoru rescued him after a car broke his leg. And eventually, though he didn’t instinctively love to be a kept cat, he became Nana and he found where he belonged. <br /><br /><i>“Our silver van was like a magic carriage. Every time I got into it, it carried me to a place I’d never been before.”</i><br /><br />Many years later Nana is taken out into the silver van on a journey to see Satoru’s friends. Each friend they visit has a story to tell about Satoru, and their love of cats, and how Satoru changed their lives. And each person learns a story from Nana. Nana visits many places, and as long as he is with Satoru, he is so happy. But Nana doesn’t yet know the real reason for their travels.<br /><br /><i>“At that moment, we were without a doubt the greatest travelers in the world. And I was the world’s greatest traveling cat.”</i><br /><br /><b>Reflection</b><br /><br />Well this is a hard book to review because I love it so much. It feels difficult to do this book justice. How many ways are there to say that this charming, magical little story will nestle into your heart and never leave? This is a book I want to reread over and over again, and continue to love and experience and learn from. This is a book about someone else’s story, but that made me think a lot about my own story.<br /><br />Let’s talk first about what it is like to read a book told to you by a cat. You’d think it would be weird, and childish. It isn’t really that way at all, though! Nana’s narration has a lot of whimsy to it, but it is anything but childish. Nana is humorous and a bit surly to strangers. Growing up as a stray has helped Nana to be tough. But he is also fiercely loyal and filled with compassion. He understands what humans need in a way that humans may not always understand it themselves. I found Nana positively delightful! I could picture him, from the figure-eight shaped calico spots on his face, to his crooked tale that led to his name. Nana is a fantastic narrator and now I wonder why all books aren’t told by cats!<br /><br />And then there is the story of Satoru, which in flashbacks we learn about him from a very young age, even before Nana. We never are told the story by Satoru himself. It is by Nana, and the friends he goes to visit, and his aunt. Despite this, Satoru is a character I feel that I know so well. Above all else, there is a kindness to Satoru that every single person could learn from. He is the sort of person that teaches other patience, kindness, and love by displaying it himself always and without expectation. I don’t imagine I will ever forget Satoru.<br /><br />I don’t want to get too much into the specifics of the visits, because each is a delight to read and experience yourself. There are so many small stories built into the life Satoru leads that warmed my heart. And Nana learns so much as well. Nana grows as a character through love and kindness, and we see the ripple effect of Satoru’s kindness throughout the novel. This is a book filled with happiness and a few tears, and I left with a smile on my face. <br /><br /><i>“On our last journey, let’s see all kinds of amazing things. Let’s spend our time taking in as many wonderful sights as we can. That’s what I had pledged yesterday, when we set off. And what incredible sights we saw.”</i><br /><br />I read this with Melissa, Berit, Holly, and Jennifer :)<br /><br />Thank you to Berkley for our copies to review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9597210196447809222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8655084-phrynne?shelf=5000-books">5000-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2255733619" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1249977976663577660">This little book is one to own in hardcover. The cover is just perfect but then I have always had a thing for black cats:)<br/><br/>The travelling cat is not black but white with patches and he really does travel around Japan with his owner Satoru. Much of the dialogue belongs to this cat and for the early part of the book I was not sure how it was going to go. It was a little slow and a little too simple but as it progressed things improved. <br/><br/>The cat called Nana (Japanese for seven because his tail was be</span>
  <span id="freeText1249977976663577660" style="display:none">This little book is one to own in hardcover. The cover is just perfect but then I have always had a thing for black cats:)<br /><br />The travelling cat is not black but white with patches and he really does travel around Japan with his owner Satoru. Much of the dialogue belongs to this cat and for the early part of the book I was not sure how it was going to go. It was a little slow and a little too simple but as it progressed things improved. <br /><br />The cat called Nana (Japanese for seven because his tail was bent like a number 7) was very intelligent even for a cat and had many profound understandings of human nature and also of the sights he saw in his travels. By the end I was completely engrossed and of course reaching for the tissues - one drawback of animal stories, they always have sad endings. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34728079.The_Travelling_Cat_Chronicles" title="The Travelling Cat Chronicles by Hiro Arikawa" rel="nofollow noopener">The Travelling Cat Chronicles</a> is very obviously a book by a Japanese author. It has a certain flow to the words and the way the characters interact reminded me very much of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3354.Haruki_Murakami" title="Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Haruki Murakami</a>. I presume it is a good translation since it reads so well. Recommended especially if you are an animal lover:)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1249977976663577660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText4181837317146751989" style="display:none">What a wonderful, petite story that I stumbled across in the bookstore the other day, and that turned out to be the most heart-warming story not only about cats, but about pets in general and how they bring joy to our lives. <br />This Japanese story played with a wish I’ve had for years: To be inside the mind of a cat and get to know what they’re thinking. Parallel to that, we’re also following the story of a cat-owner who’s desperate to find a new home for his pet. His visits to friends are entwined with flashbacks to his childhood, and all in all it makes for a wonderful story that wrapped up beautifully while my own cat happened to be sitting in my lap purring &lt;3 <br />A must-read for all cat lovers!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2568732911" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9076140607023267455">4.5 STARS<br/><br/><br/><em>
  <strong>A gentle, quiet story with the voice of a previously stray cat who has a lot of charm and a little "catitude"...</strong>
</em><br/><br/>This book is translated from Japanese and has been a best-seller in Japan.  Satoru Miyawaki meets and rescues the cat he ultimately names "Nana" even though he is a male cat.<br/><br/>Nana the cat has a crooked black tail and a white body with a little black mark on his head. He is a stray and has been living on the street.  He has taken up residence on the hood of Satoru's van. We </span>
  <span id="freeText9076140607023267455" style="display:none">4.5 STARS<br /><br /><br /><em>
  <strong>A gentle, quiet story with the voice of a previously stray cat who has a lot of charm and a little "catitude"...</strong>
</em><br /><br />This book is translated from Japanese and has been a best-seller in Japan.  Satoru Miyawaki meets and rescues the cat he ultimately names "Nana" even though he is a male cat.<br /><br />Nana the cat has a crooked black tail and a white body with a little black mark on his head. He is a stray and has been living on the street.  He has taken up residence on the hood of Satoru's van. We get to hear the POV from Nana which made this a quirky and inspirational little read. Cats are so mysterious and often quiet or with attitude.  It was just fun to hear from this wise and loving little cat! He did steal my heart &lt;3<br /><br />While reading I kept wondering why Satoru was trying to find his beloved Nana a new home, and I was worried for him. You'll have to read it to find out the details.  My heart did skip a few beats, but all is well.<br /><br />I loved the story and the message. Cat lovers will especially enjoy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9076140607023267455" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2522526229" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2522526229" />
    <a title="~Bookishly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28323108-bookishly"><img alt="~Bookishly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605967142p2/28323108.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2522526229?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Bookishly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Bookishly" href="/user/show/28323108-bookishly">~Bookishly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34728079-the-travelling-cat-chronicles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28323108-bookishly?shelf=bleh">bleh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2522526229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6914207956874042885">As a fellow cat lover, I actually feel a pang of guilt, for giving this book a low rating. This was just not what I expected and it was just such a tiresome read. In a nutshell, this is a rather twee story about a man and his cat. We get taken on a road trip, travel around a bit, but overall, it all got a bit predictable for my liking. I mean, I had already guessed what was going to happen in the first few chapters. <br/>This was apparently a tear-jerking read, but for me, the only tears I was sheddi</span>
  <span id="freeText6914207956874042885" style="display:none">As a fellow cat lover, I actually feel a pang of guilt, for giving this book a low rating. This was just not what I expected and it was just such a tiresome read. In a nutshell, this is a rather twee story about a man and his cat. We get taken on a road trip, travel around a bit, but overall, it all got a bit predictable for my liking. I mean, I had already guessed what was going to happen in the first few chapters. <br />This was apparently a tear-jerking read, but for me, the only tears I was shedding, were ones caused by my excessive yawning. I suppose after reading many reviews that had a great deal of praise for this book, I was expecting my heart to be broken somewhat, but after finishing the book, I feel nothing, and I've already forgotten the story. And no, I cannot understand why others would be moved to tears with this book, I really can't. <br />The characters themselves, are fairly mediocre. The cat is flat and boring, and it all gets slightly ridiculous when it begins talking to other animals like we would have a conversation. The biggest problem for me, which stood out a mile, was the simpleness of the writing. I don't know whether that was to do with the translation, but it was too simple and average for me. <br />Believe me now, my heart is breakable, but this was way too hyped, and definitely didn't live up to my expectations. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6914207956874042885" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2171359063" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2171359063" />
    <a title="Nat K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35251024-nat-k"><img alt="Nat K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577481825p2/35251024.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2171359063?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat K" href="/user/show/35251024-nat-k">Nat K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34728079-the-travelling-cat-chronicles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35251024-nat-k?shelf=animal-magic">animal-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35251024-nat-k?shelf=bookclub-2018">bookclub-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35251024-nat-k?shelf=2018-books">2018-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35251024-nat-k?shelf=friends-and-family">friends-and-family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35251024-nat-k?shelf=japonais">japonais</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35251024-nat-k?shelf=feline-magic">feline-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35251024-nat-k?shelf=heartstrings">heartstrings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35251024-nat-k?shelf=life-is-a-curious-thing">life-is-a-curious-thing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35251024-nat-k?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2171359063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16790260520553192840">Sometimes the gentler stories have the biggest impact. My heart has melted!<br/><br/>A beautiful jewel of story, a delightful gem.<br/><br/>A heartwarming tale of the relationship between a young man Sukoru, and his cat Nana (a stray that he rescues after being run over). But this is over simplifying a story which has <u>so many</u> layers to it.<br/><br/><i>”And so began our new life together, Satoru was the perfect roommate for a cat, and I was the perfect roommate for a human.”</i><br/><br/>Sukoru and Nana live together for five happy years, whe</span>
  <span id="freeText16790260520553192840" style="display:none">Sometimes the gentler stories have the biggest impact. My heart has melted!<br /><br />A beautiful jewel of story, a delightful gem.<br /><br />A heartwarming tale of the relationship between a young man Sukoru, and his cat Nana (a stray that he rescues after being run over). But this is over simplifying a story which has <u>so many</u> layers to it.<br /><br /><i>”And so began our new life together, Satoru was the perfect roommate for a cat, and I was the perfect roommate for a human.”</i><br /><br />Sukoru and Nana live together for five happy years, when things change and Sukoru has to find a new owner to love and care for Nana…this is where the “travelling” part of the story comes into the equation, as Nana &amp; Sukoru travel in his silver van across the countryside, revisiting long lost friends in their quest.<br /><br /><i>”Our silver van was like a magic carriage. Every time I got into it, it carried me to a place I’d never been before. At that moment, we were without a doubt the greatest travellers in the world. And I was the world’s greatest travelling cat.”</i><br /><br />There are insights into family, friendships, life, love &amp; loss. All revealed a bit a time. Yes, this is a tear-jerker. But it’s oh-so-worth-it. And there are happy tears too, as I think this story ended gorgeously, with a tone of hope and redemption about the circle of life.<br /><br />The voice of Nana is feisty and often wise-cracking. I really enjoy books which tell their story (or part of) from an animal’s point of view. They are sentient creatures and far more aware of goings on than we give them credit for.<br /><br /><i>”Humans who think we don’t understand them are the stupid ones.”</i><br /><br />And the character of Sukoru is a delightful. A cheerful young man, who should be anything but, considering the cards that have been dealt him.<br /><br />If the rainbow scene towards the end of the story doesn’t put a lump in your throat, please check for a pulse! <br /><br />Dare I say purr-fection in its simplicity. Grab your favourite cuppa, turn the phone to silent, and open your heart. You won’t be disappointed.<br />😻<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16790260520553192840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2536913566" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2536913566" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5211606-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505571524p2/5211606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2536913566?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/5211606-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5211606-julie?shelf=giveaways">giveaways</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5211606-julie?shelf=i-think-i-m-turning-japanese">i-think-i-m-turning-japanese</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2536913566" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13858537811655677678">English is my native language, but I grew up in the Miami area, so when it came time to choose a second language, I went with Spanish.<br/><br/>I loved learning Spanish, and I was especially thrilled that it helped me become an expert at ordering my most favorite indulgence: Cuban coffee.<br/><br/>But, my moment of crowning achievement with the language was the day when I was handed Sr. Marquez's <i>El Coronel No Tiene Quien Le Escriba</i>, and I read it.<br/><br/>I read it. And, like, I couldn't believe it. I read Marquez <i>in Spani</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13858537811655677678" style="display:none">English is my native language, but I grew up in the Miami area, so when it came time to choose a second language, I went with Spanish.<br /><br />I loved learning Spanish, and I was especially thrilled that it helped me become an expert at ordering my most favorite indulgence: Cuban coffee.<br /><br />But, my moment of crowning achievement with the language was the day when I was handed Sr. Marquez's <i>El Coronel No Tiene Quien Le Escriba</i>, and I read it.<br /><br />I read it. And, like, I couldn't believe it. I read Marquez <i>in Spanish</i>, as it was truly meant to be read. . . and I was like. . . whoa. . . damn it. . . it's so different, when pieces of meaning aren't lost in translation!!<br /><br />I then added Pablo Neruda's poetry in Spanish. . . and <i>mierda</i>. . . and <i>dios mio</i>!! It's even more freaking fantastic! <br /><br />Sadly, Spanish is the only other language I can really read in, but it was such an eye opener for me. SO MUCH IS LOST IN TRANSLATION, y'all. . . SO MUCH.<br /><br />And that's about ALL I could think about as I read this recently translated novel out of Japan.<br /><br />This little book, <i>The Travelling Cat Chronicles</i>, is a bestseller in Japan and is hitting book stores here in the U.S. on October 23.<br /><br />From what I can determine from reviews on here, it received a warmer reception from my reviewing friends than it did from me.<br /><br />I just kept getting stuck, tripping over the stilted cadence of the awkwardly translated passages. Why are a group of thirty-somethings in Japan using words like: reckon, dodgy and glum?<br /><br />These are Nancy Drew words, people. Words that you can find in the first book of the Nancy Drew series, <i>The Secret of the Old Clock</i>, originally published in 1930. Other words of this time period include: famished, pell-mell and sulk. <br /><br />It is very uncommon to hear or read any these words today. At least here, in the U.S., among people younger than, say, 80. In fact, when I read Nancy Drew books to my girls now, they often have no idea what I'm saying, and I must update many of the expressions.<br /><br />Language moves. It shifts. It rarely remains stagnant. <br /><br />If I wrote a poem in Spanish right now, my own language would possibly be out-of-date. I haven't stayed current in that language, and my regular diet of Marquez and Neruda doesn't help me stay current with Spanish expressions.<br /><br />This little book, told from a cat's perspective (another unfortunate aspect for me), felt stodgy to me.<br /><br />And, in case you're unclear. . . <i>stodgy</i> is a word no longer in regular use in the U.S., either.<br /><br /><i>I would like to express gratitude to Berkley Publishing for your generosity in providing me with an arc</i>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13858537811655677678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780857524188" href="/book/show/34211804-the-travelling-cat-chronicles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=animal-stories">animal-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19559507-carolyn?shelf=around-the-world">around-the-world</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2169238205" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1201502342041470154">Although I bought this book for the cover - a painting of a little black cat that looks so like my current sweet cat - it is also turned out to be a most delightful read as well.<br/> <br/>Nana, the cat in the story is white with black splotches and a tail bent like a number seven (nana in Japanese). He starts life growing up on the streets and makes friends with Satoru when he starts to leave him food under his silver van. When Nana is hurt in an accident Satoru nurses him back to health and Nana decides</span>
  <span id="freeText1201502342041470154" style="display:none">Although I bought this book for the cover - a painting of a little black cat that looks so like my current sweet cat - it is also turned out to be a most delightful read as well.<br /> <br />Nana, the cat in the story is white with black splotches and a tail bent like a number seven (nana in Japanese). He starts life growing up on the streets and makes friends with Satoru when he starts to leave him food under his silver van. When Nana is hurt in an accident Satoru nurses him back to health and Nana decides to stay with him. After a few years together Satoru takes Nana on trips in his van to meet old friends with the plan of finding Nana a new home. Nana is puzzled by this but enjoys the travel to new places and the journey through Satoru's past until he realises the reason why Satoru is trying to find his beloved cat a new home.<br /> <br />Told through Satoru's and Nana's eyes, this is a bitter-sweet story of a loving, gentle man, his friendships and life and his love for his cat. Nana has a voice that is direct and sometimes snarky and the story of their travels and the people and animals and people they meet is told with humour as well as tenderness and love. A deceptively simple tale, beautifully translated, that left me just a little teary. 4.5★</span>
  <a data-text-id="1201502342041470154" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2480266808" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2480266808" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4125660-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316269997p2/4125660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2480266808?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/4125660-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4125660-liz?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2480266808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8344452303654589803"><br/>I’m a dog person, but really, if you love a pet, it’s the same. So, I decided to give this small book about a cat and his person a shot. Nana is a feral cat when we first meet him. But a broken leg transforms him into Satoru’s pet. When Satoru says he must give up Nana for some unknown reason, they start off on a road trip, trying to find the right home for Nana. <br/><br/>Be aware, Nana is the narrator of this tale. If you have trouble with anthropomorphism, this will not be the book for you. <br/><br/>This is a v</span>
  <span id="freeText8344452303654589803" style="display:none"><br />I’m a dog person, but really, if you love a pet, it’s the same. So, I decided to give this small book about a cat and his person a shot. Nana is a feral cat when we first meet him. But a broken leg transforms him into Satoru’s pet. When Satoru says he must give up Nana for some unknown reason, they start off on a road trip, trying to find the right home for Nana. <br /><br />Be aware, Nana is the narrator of this tale. If you have trouble with anthropomorphism, this will not be the book for you. <br /><br />This is a very understated, slow moving book. As Satoru and Nana travel from friend to friend, we learn more of Satoru’s boyhood. And it doesn’t take much imagination to figure out the reason for the road trip. The ending is bittersweet. I’ll admit to crying, because it did hit perfectly on the love between a human and our four legged companions. But, in the end, it was just a little too low key for my taste. <br /><br />The writing is fairly elementary but I’m not sure if that’s because it’s a translation from the original Japanese. <br /><br />My thanks to netgalley and Berkley Publishing for an advance copy of this book<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8344452303654589803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3070330990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8453633312377205859">❤️BELOVED❤️<br/><br/><br/>Every page of this precious book counts for pleasure:<br/>If you’re a pet owner you’ll immediately recognize the unique feeling that comes from the pleasant relation we share (yes: we! I happen to be a quite happy member of the pet owners club!) with our beloved pets 🥰 .<br/><br/>On the other hand, if you’re a non-pet-owner, you’ll probably end up facing a 2 options menu:<br/>1 - Going to the nearest pet shop to gift yourself the loveliest pet<br/>2 - Not gifting yourself a pet, and... as a result... you’ll b</span>
  <span id="freeText8453633312377205859" style="display:none">❤️BELOVED❤️<br /><br /><br />Every page of this precious book counts for pleasure:<br />If you’re a pet owner you’ll immediately recognize the unique feeling that comes from the pleasant relation we share (yes: we! I happen to be a quite happy member of the pet owners club!) with our beloved pets 🥰 .<br /><br />On the other hand, if you’re a non-pet-owner, you’ll probably end up facing a 2 options menu:<br />1 - Going to the nearest pet shop to gift yourself the loveliest pet<br />2 - Not gifting yourself a pet, and... as a result... you’ll be doomed to a forever jealousy feeling (jealousy from what won’t take you much long to find out...😉)<br /><br />Yes! This book will do that to you! Please allow yourself the pleasure of reading it!!!🥰</span>

<div id="review_2170483082" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2170483082" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28602001-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438967931p2/28602001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2170483082?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/28602001-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/34728079-the-travelling-cat-chronicles">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28602001-emma?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2170483082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2407017610029394468">Translated from the Japanese, this tale of the relationship between Satoru Miyawaki and Nana, the injured stray cat he nurses back to health, is both heartwarming and achingly sad. <br/><br/>Told from both perspectives, it was somewhat disconcerting at first, but very soon pulled me even more deeply into the story. Nana can be a particularly snarky animal when the situation calls for it and his commentary provides some much needed humour, especially as the mystery of just why Satoru is trying to find him </span>
  <span id="freeText2407017610029394468" style="display:none">Translated from the Japanese, this tale of the relationship between Satoru Miyawaki and Nana, the injured stray cat he nurses back to health, is both heartwarming and achingly sad. <br /><br />Told from both perspectives, it was somewhat disconcerting at first, but very soon pulled me even more deeply into the story. Nana can be a particularly snarky animal when the situation calls for it and his commentary provides some much needed humour, especially as the mystery of just why Satoru is trying to find him another home becomes ever more clear. <br /><br />Their journey across the beautiful Japanese landscape takes one man and his cat into the past, meeting childhood companions in a celebration of their first meetings and long friendship. With each stop a new tale is woven, another aspect of Satoru's life joyously recounted, while in the present day, both Satoru and Nana decide whether <i>this</i> will be the cat's new home. Yet Nana knows his place is with the human he loves beyond all others and is more than prepared to do what it takes to stay with him till the end.<br /><br />A truly beautiful account of friendships and love, both human and feline, that will stay with you. I finished reading it with tears rolling past my smile, what greater accolade could I give to this wonderful little book?<br /><br /><br />ARC via Netgalley</span>
  <a data-text-id="2407017610029394468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PXz509hRHPnBZc9xiNn97f5wo36e+DNxrLJ9TEbk8/+IgDAMOi3hOPZatTACOwBUisEhnqLVOeHHHCTpISPxig==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yZFsv1CbpRYefc1XiD/AAFpeIDv1TLMIfRxYpmw8vnl8baVgsudY1ylCtxYC3T25Lu+i28lhuZgWsgEDC/u8DA==')})
  }

But this coffee shop offers its customers a unique experience: the chance to travel back in time.\n\nIn Before the Coffee Gets Cold, we meet four visitors, each of whom is hoping to make use of the café’s time-travelling offer, in order to: confront the man who left them, receive a letter from their husband whose memory has been taken by early onset Alzheimer\'s, to see their sister one last time, and to meet the daughter they never got the chance to know.\n\nBut the journey into the past does not come without risks: customers must sit in a particular seat, they cannot leave the café, and finally, they must return to the present before the coffee gets cold . . .\n\nToshikazu Kawaguchi’s beautiful, moving story explores the age-old question: what would you change if you could travel back in time? Keiko has never fit in, neither in her family, nor in school, but when at the age of eighteen she begins working at the Hiiromachi branch of “Smile Mart,” she finds peace and purpose in her life. In the store, unlike anywhere else, she understands the rules of social interaction ― many are laid out line by line in the store’s manual ― and she does her best to copy the dress, mannerisms, and speech of her colleagues, playing the part of a “normal” person excellently, more or less. Managers come and go, but Keiko stays at the store for eighteen years. It’s almost hard to tell where the store ends and she begins. Keiko is very happy, but the people close to her, from her family to her coworkers, increasingly pressure her to find a husband, and to start a proper career, prompting her to take desperate action…\nA brilliant depiction of an unusual psyche and a world hidden from view, Convenience Store Woman is an ironic and sharp-eyed look at contemporary work culture and the pressures to conform, as       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4823030.Hiro_Arikawa">About Hiro Arikawa</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4823030.Hiro_Arikawa"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1553387795p3/4823030.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/4823030.Hiro_Arikawa">Hiro Arikawa
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
414
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer14574630193332976509">Hiro Arikawa won the tenth annual Dengeki Novel Prize for new writers for Shio no Machi: Wish on My Precious in 2003, and the book was published the following year. It was praised for its love story between a heroine and hero divided by age and social status, and for its depiction of military structures. Although she is a light novelist, her books from her second work onwards have been published a</span>
  <span id="freeText14574630193332976509" style="display:none">Hiro Arikawa won the tenth annual Dengeki Novel Prize for new writers for Shio no Machi: Wish on My Precious in 2003, and the book was published the following year. It was praised for its love story between a heroine and hero divided by age and social status, and for its depiction of military structures. Although she is a light novelist, her books from her second work onwards have been published as hardbacks alongside more literary works with Arikawa receiving special treatment in this respect from her publisher, MediaWorks. Shio no Machi was also later published in hardback. Her 2006 light novel Toshokan Sensō (The Library War) was named as Hon no Zasshi's number one for entertainment for the first half of 2006, and came fifth in the Honya Taishō for that year, competing against ordinary novels.<br /><br />She often writes about the Japan Self-Defense Forces (JSDF) and her first three novels concerning its three branches are known as the Jieitai Sanbusaku (The SDF Trilogy); she also wrote about the fictional Library Forces in the Toshokan Sensō series. Raintree no Kuni, which first appeared as a book within a book in Toshokan Nairan was later published by Arikawa as a spin-off with another publisher. It was adapted into a film titled World of Delight released on November 21, 2015.[2][3]Her novel Shokubutsu Zukan (ja) will be adapted into a film titled Shokubutsu Zukan: Unmei no Koi, Hiroimashita and scheduled for release on June 4, 2016.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14574630193332976509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
